    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706263298" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=thanks-for-prezzies">thanks-for-prezzies</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer706263298" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer924043953016375856">i got this wonderful book from connor for my birrrtthhddaaayyy!!!<br/><br/>and it is yet another book that is beautiful enough that even had its contents been crappy, i would still love just to hold it and heft it and appreciate the texture and weight of it. it is from a small publisher whose motto is "publish few but wonderful books." <br/><br/>see for yourself:<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.sortof.co.uk/'>http://www.sortof.co.uk/</a><br/><br/>this is the first ever moomin book, published in 1945. it was out of print for forever, then reprinted in 1991, and then re-reprint</span>
  <span id="freeText924043953016375856" style="display:none">i got this wonderful book from connor for my birrrtthhddaaayyy!!!<br><br>and it is yet another book that is beautiful enough that even had its contents been crappy, i would still love just to hold it and heft it and appreciate the texture and weight of it. it is from a small publisher whose motto is "publish few but wonderful books." <br><br>see for yourself:<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sortof.co.uk/">http://www.sortof.co.uk/</a><br><br>this is the first ever moomin book, published in 1945. it was out of print for forever, then reprinted in 1991, and then re-reprinted in 2012. and now i has it. <br><br>the story itself is meandering and simple and dreamlike, but coupled with these amazing illustrations, it is hard not to love it like candy:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03444_zpsa39a7acc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877719._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03444_zpsa39a7acc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>i love the way the moomin characters look in this book - they are just rough sketches of what would later evolve into the more round and sweet and familiar moomins of the later books.<br><br>from:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03443_zps46868fc8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877720._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03443_zps46868fc8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877721._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>throughout the book, the artwork is split between very simple line drawings:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03442_zps65397392.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877722._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03442_zps65397392.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>to these amazing sepia watercolors:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03441_zpscbb8af92.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877723._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03441_zpscbb8af92.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>the story takes the shape of a journey by moominmamma and baby moomintroll to find where moominpappa, last seen in the company of the hattifatteners, has gotten himself off to. along the way, they meet other characters who will later become moomin "regulars" and moomintroll will eat too much candy in a sort of willy wonka-type wonderland.<br><br>also, there will be cats:<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03445_zps9319f5d6.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877724._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03445_zps9319f5d6.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03446_zps0f6fffa8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877725._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03446_zps0f6fffa8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>it's just a wonderful, magical book in which all the moominroots can be seen and it is charming and sweet but also very dark, as all the best children's books are.<br><br>this is my favorite drawing on the book, because of how simple and delicate and and innocent and evocative it is. this, to me, is just lovely.<br><br><a href="http://s1131.photobucket.com/user/kettincat/media/aifaf%202013/DSC03448_zps1f0c92b1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877726._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo DSC03448_zps1f0c92b1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>if you have never read a moomin book, change that now. they are perfect little jewels of creatures and everyone should have them in their hearts. whe!<br><br>tove jansson and friends:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434710i/877727.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>

<div id="review_485579938" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485579938" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/343944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242156693p2/343944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/343944-emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485579938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13625016197334926148">On no account should anyone trying Tove Jansson for the first time start with this book, the original Moomin story, published in 1945 and recently translated into English for the very first time. Because of course there's a reason <i>why</i> it was untranslated all these years (and, additionally, out of print in the original Swedish); it's just not that good. The art work is charming, but the story, which is quite short, is just kind of random, helterskelter, and unsatisfying. That being said, it's a m</span>
  <span id="freeText13625016197334926148" style="display:none">On no account should anyone trying Tove Jansson for the first time start with this book, the original Moomin story, published in 1945 and recently translated into English for the very first time. Because of course there's a reason <i>why</i> it was untranslated all these years (and, additionally, out of print in the original Swedish); it's just not that good. The art work is charming, but the story, which is quite short, is just kind of random, helterskelter, and unsatisfying. That being said, it's a must for Moomin completists, and for me personally, just learning of the existence of this book was satisfying in that I finally understood what flood was being referred to at the beginning of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1003725.Comet_in_Moominland__The_Moomins___2_" title="Comet in Moominland (The Moomins, #2) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Comet in Moominland</a>, which used to be considered book 1. As a child I thought Jansson was referring to the one in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/682596.Moominsummer_Madness__The_Moomins___5_" title="Moominsummer Madness (The Moomins, #5) by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">Moominsummer Madness</a>, a later book in the series, and was deeply confused about the time frame of the books, which, for a time, rather put me off the moomins until I was older and better able to cope with ambiguity!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13625016197334926148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2364799413342952067" style="display:none">I had heard of Tove Jansson and her Moomins, but that was pretty much the extent of my knowledge. It was therefore a lovely surprise to discover this fairy tale, featuring Moomintroll and Moominmamma in their search for a place to live and their long lost Moominpappa. <br><br>The writing is simple but not devoid of lyricism. Being a translation, I can but wonder at how the original text feels, and if this is even more pronounced. The story follows a âtypicalâ search with mini adventures punctuating the narrative, some more dangerous than others, introducing us to different protagonists. It is so sweet and yet, you can feel the darker undercurrent. Tove wrote it during the WWII and published it in 1945. It is therefore not surprising that this is a âdisguisedâ tale of families divided and highlights an anxious yearning for safety in all its meanings. <br><br>What did surprise me a lot was Toveâs artistic skill! I had no idea she drew at all (I know, my bad) and her illustrations totally enchanted me. Wow! So simple in some occasions but full of feeling. Iâm in awe!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515160763i/24836145._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I donât know how this first volume compares with the rest of the series, but from a new reader, I am charmed. Iâm particularly tempted now to read her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/79550.The_Summer_Book" title="The Summer Book by Tove Jansson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Summer Book</a>.</span>

<div id="review_2095122940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2095122940" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095122940?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=magical-creatures">magical-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=moomins">moomins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=fairy-tales-fantasy">fairy-tales-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=translations">translations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095122940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11694359319007170450">When I was a child and read Tove Jansson's evocative and adventurous tale of how a comet threatens the Moomins and their valley (<u>Comet in Moominland</u>, although I actually read it in German), I was rather annoyed and frustrated with and by the fact that while there were all these textual allusions and hints at the beginning of <u>Comet in Moominland</u> of there having previously been a massive flooding, the novel where this so-called Great Flood occurs had never been translated from its original Swedish</span>
  <span id="freeText11694359319007170450" style="display:none">When I was a child and read Tove Jansson's evocative and adventurous tale of how a comet threatens the Moomins and their valley (<u>Comet in Moominland</u>, although I actually read it in German), I was rather annoyed and frustrated with and by the fact that while there were all these textual allusions and hints at the beginning of <u>Comet in Moominland</u> of there having previously been a massive flooding, the novel where this so-called Great Flood occurs had never been translated from its original Swedish (finally remedied in 2006 with this here English language translation by David McDuff).<br /><br />And after now after having read <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u>, I can certainly and very much understand why this novel (which is considered the first Moomin tale and was orignally published in 1945, and was also for decades out of print even in its Swedish original), has only recently been translated (the simple fact being that although author and illustrator Tove Jansson's accompanying pictorial images are indeed glowingly descriptive, esoteric and for all intents and purposes wonderful, the actual text, the actual featured narrative, the story of <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u> is simply, is just not in any way en par with the other Moomin novels). For the text feels majorly choppy, uneven and often so bare bones that one might almost assume one is reading more of an outline of a novel than an actual and finished, polished end product. I mean, we as readers never really do manage to obtain all that much knowledge and information as to exactly why Moominpapa has ended up being missing. Yes, he has seemingly abandoned his family (his wife and young son) to travel with the Hatifatners, but no detailed and specific reasons as to why are ever really textually given. And even the Great Flood itself is at least in my opinion rather a non event, is presented by Jansson as being there, being a presence, but with only scant description and portrayal (which also and indeed seems to be the case with almost all of the diverse episodes of <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u>, the featured and presented nuggets of detail and of even storytelling charm, pieces of information that seem important for a short while but then like a flame, sputtering out, failing to coalesce into a harmonious whole). <br /><br />And thus, while I do appreciate finally having had the opportunity to read, to experience Tove Jansson's very first Moomin book and cheer the fact that her <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u> was in 2006 translated from the original Swedish into English (as well as subsequently into other languages), is again in print and as available as the rest of the Moomin series (since it does in fact clean up some loose ends and presents how the Moomins originally reach their valley, and also how they meet and in many ways become saddled with the intriguing and sometimes a trifle frustrating kangaroo-like creature who in the later Moomin novels is known as Sniff), I still have found <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u> only rather very mildly amusing and entertaining at best, and the novel's general writing style, its textual authorial presentation too scattered, too unfinished and too unpolished to be considered with more than two stars (and leave the truth and caveat that the sequels are definitely much superior and are to be in all ways preferred and recommended above <u>The Moomins and the Great Flood</u> which I really would only suggest for serious Moomin series fans and completists).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11694359319007170450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2978911138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2978911138" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2978911138?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2978911138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8259782236683953215">To be honest, I've never really thought much of reading or watching anything from the <i>Moomin</i> series until I bought this book. It's not that I didn't think I would like it, but in spite of the huge fan culture surrounding it, it was a series which just kept slipping my mind. I also had no idea that it was as old as it was. I had always assumed it was a product of the 1980's, but it turns out its roots go much earlier. <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> was, from my understanding, from the 1940's. <br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText8259782236683953215" style="display:none">To be honest, I've never really thought much of reading or watching anything from the <i>Moomin</i> series until I bought this book. It's not that I didn't think I would like it, but in spite of the huge fan culture surrounding it, it was a series which just kept slipping my mind. I also had no idea that it was as old as it was. I had always assumed it was a product of the 1980's, but it turns out its roots go much earlier. <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> was, from my understanding, from the 1940's. <br /><br />This is a pretty basic fantasy story, but it's also visually beautiful and full of whimsical characters, benevolent wit and cute absurdity which makes it a great and fun story for readers of all ages. It has the right balance of dark and light in terms of a plot, but it isn't so dark that it can't be enjoyed by younger readers. Its greatest asset is in its variety of simplistic, beautiful illustrations, done in paintings as well as line drawings, distinguishing not only the characters themselves, but also the charming and at times mysterious world they live in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8259782236683953215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1140867429" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2986584654822955951">I loves me some Moomins!<br/>This is the original story, coming in 1945 before the comic strip or the first of the famous novels, Comet in Moominland. It has none of the satire of either of the former but it does have the same bizarre, delightful, magical world of strange creatures and peculiar adventures, featuring everybody's favourite troll family. Speaking of delightful, Jansson's illustrations are as wonderful and playful as you would expect. This edition is an inexpensive fairly large format ha</span>
  <span id="freeText2986584654822955951" style="display:none">I loves me some Moomins!<br />This is the original story, coming in 1945 before the comic strip or the first of the famous novels, Comet in Moominland. It has none of the satire of either of the former but it does have the same bizarre, delightful, magical world of strange creatures and peculiar adventures, featuring everybody's favourite troll family. Speaking of delightful, Jansson's illustrations are as wonderful and playful as you would expect. This edition is an inexpensive fairly large format hardback that allows for reprinting said illustrations at a size worthy of them and in superior quality, too. It's a quick, fun read, a short story even by kiddy standards, excellent for filling in a moment when I was unable to focus sufficiently for my more demanding current reading projects.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer825582299049143456">#2016-aty-reading-challenge-week-30: A fairytale from a culture other than your own.<br/><br/>The first of the Moomin fairytales by the Scandinavian author, Tove Jansson, is quite charming. Moomintroll and his mama set off on an odyssey to find a nice sunny place where they can build a house. Along the way, they make new friends, face dangers and reunite with Moominpappa. A timeless children's classic. </span>

<div id="review_567462760" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/567462760" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2631425-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538808870p2/2631425.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/567462760?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/2631425-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781908745132" href="/book/show/16169056-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=illustrated">illustrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=film-and-tv">film-and-tv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2631425-michael?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer567462760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4330525794730293285">I remember Moomintroll from TV adaptations and Jackanory readings from when I was a child, but I've never read any of Jansson's Moomin stories until now. I liked it!<br/><br/>The story has its interesting points, but what makes this book for me are Jansson's illustrations - very strange, phantasmagorical and other-worldly.<br/><br/>The slim story is a series of episodes in the journey made by Moomintroll and Moominmamma, searching for the missing Moominpappa who, for no good reason that I can discern, has left his </span>
  <span id="freeText4330525794730293285" style="display:none">I remember Moomintroll from TV adaptations and Jackanory readings from when I was a child, but I've never read any of Jansson's Moomin stories until now. I liked it!<br /><br />The story has its interesting points, but what makes this book for me are Jansson's illustrations - very strange, phantasmagorical and other-worldly.<br /><br />The slim story is a series of episodes in the journey made by Moomintroll and Moominmamma, searching for the missing Moominpappa who, for no good reason that I can discern, has left his family to go a-wandering with the rather creepy Hattifatners. The "little creature" they meet and adopt (named Sniff in later books) is reminiscent of Piglet, Winnie-the-Pooh's friend, being easily frightened and rather timorous through most of the story. Tulippa is a rather mysterious "flower-fairy", who joins their company for a while, before somewhat capriciously deciding to shack up with a lighthouse keeper (if it was a lighthouse). Then there's the old man who has created a world made out of chocolates (Fazer brand), sweets and lemonade, prefiguring Dahl's Willy Wonka, though I'm uncertain as to any direct connection.<br /><br />A great story for children, and I'm sorry that I didn't come to these books in time to read them to mine - I think I've a while to wait for grandchildren, but when they arrive Moomintroll will be waiting for them!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4330525794730293285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17390845757043964261" style="display:none">As someone who grew up in Sweden, the Moomins have always been a part of my childhood. I watched the TV series with my parents because they were a bit too scary sometimes. I went to the library to borrow the computer games and sat in our closet, building ice castles with Moomin. But I realised that I never read the books, therefore I decided that I should read them. <br /><br />This is the first in the series and it's a really short book. I've heard a lot of people saying that this is the least good in the series. It's simply short and sweet, and the art work is lovely! But I feel like you can skip this and start on the second book as well, since this is more like a random story which brings an introduction to the Moomins.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5711017718211274364">As with all of Tove Jansson's work, <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> is an absolute delight. I chose to reread it during the summer, and gloried once more in its beautiful illustrations, and its inventive story. The artwork here is both whimsical and dark, and sets the tone wonderfully. Immersive and glorious.</span>

<div id="review_2153920660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153920660" />
    <a title="Girl with her Head in a Book" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14037242-girl-with-her-head-in-a-book"><img alt="Girl with her Head in a Book" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351676097p2/14037242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153920660?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Girl with her Head in a Book" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Girl with her Head in a Book" href="/user/show/14037242-girl-with-her-head-in-a-book">Girl with her Head in a Book</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14037242-girl-with-her-head-in-a-book?shelf=moomins">moomins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14037242-girl-with-her-head-in-a-book?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14037242-girl-with-her-head-in-a-book?shelf=picture-book">picture-book</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153920660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5351344617841769980">For my full review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://girlwithherheadinabook.co.uk/2017/12/review-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood-tove-jansson.html'>http://girlwithherheadinabook.co.uk/2...</a><br/><br/>2017 has been the year of my Moomins Renaissance , inspired in no small part by my visit to the exhibition in the Southbank Centre which really helped to put the background mythology of the series into context.Â  Like all of the best literature written for children, it can be just as easily enjoyed by adults.Â  As long as you can actually get hold of it of course - despite being the first story written,Â The Moomins and the Great FloodÂ was</span>
  <span id="freeText5351344617841769980" style="display:none">For my full review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://girlwithherheadinabook.co.uk/2017/12/review-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood-tove-jansson.html">http://girlwithherheadinabook.co.uk/2...</a><br /><br />2017 has been the year of my Moomins Renaissance , inspired in no small part by my visit to the exhibition in the Southbank Centre which really helped to put the background mythology of the series into context.Â  Like all of the best literature written for children, it can be just as easily enjoyed by adults.Â  As long as you can actually get hold of it of course - despite being the first story written,Â The Moomins and the Great FloodÂ was not translated into English until 2005 and this edition was only released by Sort Of Books in 2012.Â  Having finally tracked down a copy, it was with delight that I settled down to actually read it.Â  I was not disappointed.<br /><br />Beautifully illustrated with Jansson's original full-colour watercolours,Â The Moomins and the Great FloodÂ showcases Jansson as an artist more so than any of its sibling stories.Â  It also had a greater fairytale feel, even opening with the words 'Once Upon a Time' and telling the story of a little Moomintroll and his mother looking through the woods for his lost father.Â  Moominmamma feels incomplete without her spouse and the figure of the always self-centred Sniff does not yet seem quite like himself, referred to as 'the little creature'.<br /><br />With many of the most familiar characters not introduced untilÂ Comet in Moominland, this story has the note of a prelude, of Jansson still finding her story.Â  Even the illustrations themselves show subtle differences, with the snouts of the Moomins being slightly narrower.Â  There is also none of the typical humour or satire, but Jansson was in a very different place emotionally when she first sat down to create the Moomins.<br /><br />As with all Moomin-related media, a darker tale lurks beneath the surface.Â  First published in 1945 and written during the war period,Â The Moomins and the Great FloodÂ is a tale of displaced people, divided families and the desperate yearning to find a home.Â  Jansson was herself deeply anxious and very depressed during this time and it is natural that this should be expressed through her work.Â  Even as a child, I always found the Hattifattener figures to be very unnerving and here, their first canonical appearance, they appear almost like zombies.Â  Even the usually level-headed Moominmamma grows frustrated with their blank lack of expression.Â  What does the Hattifattener figure really mean?Â  Are their blank inert faces the depiction of trauma?Â  Or do they represent people who shut their eyes and ears to what was happening to those around them?<br /><br />Despite the melancholy, Great FloodÂ is still taking the reader towards a good place and we get the ending that we expect and deserve -Â the family is reunited and all ready to set up home in Moominhouse, which is built in the shape of a round stove, a reference to the stoves that moomintrolls used to live in until the advent of central heating.Â  Despite the suggestions of despair through the story, there is still a consistent thread of reassurance in the shape of Moominmamma - her handbag will nearly always have a solution and her arms are always open to any creature in distress.Â  There are times when even as an adult I would love to have someone like her to turn to.<br /><br />I adored the Moomins as a child but with with so few of the books in print in English back then, I was reduced to readingÂ Finn Family MoomintrollÂ repeatedly and always with the vague feeling that some part of the story was missing, with so many references to past events that I felt I was supposed to understand.Â  It has been a lot of fun this year going back through to find the missing pieces of the Moomin puzzle.Â  On every level, the books are beautiful - Philip Pullman describes them as 'the perfect marriage of word and picture' and that is such an apt description.Â  Without the words, this is a cartoon strip about a group of tiny hippos going on an adventure.Â  Without the pictures, we have an incomprehensible jumble of made-up words behaving eccentrically.Â  United, we have magic.<br /><br />With the cast not yet quite gathered,Â Great Flood is not peak-Moomin material - I particularly missed Snufkin - but it nonetheless a lovely addition to the canon.Â  PerhapsÂ CometÂ orÂ Finn Family may serve as a better introduction for new fansÂ  but established followers of the story will not wish to miss out on the Moomin origin story.Â  There is always something deeply comforting about returning to Moominvalley and it is reassuring to know that this feeling was present in the stories from the moment Jansson first put pen to paper.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5351344617841769980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1306664828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306664828" />
    <a title="Antonomasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6249204-antonomasia"><img alt="Antonomasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605185148p2/6249204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306664828?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antonomasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antonomasia" href="/user/show/6249204-antonomasia">Antonomasia</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781908745149" href="/book/show/21898487-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=nordic">nordic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=women-in-translation">women-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=decade-1940s">decade-1940s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6249204-antonomasia?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306664828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13669010674651156443">Read now because of the blog event Women in Translation Month.<br/><br/>I don't really know Moomin characters like many of you do: I didn't see a Moomin book until the age of 7 or 8 (and remember realising these were the Moomin things some of the other kids had been talking about) By then, they looked a bit 'babyish'. I read the then-available books very quickly and often once only. <br/><br/>So reading this - recently translated to English for the first time - I had little to no idea of how different the character</span>
  <span id="freeText13669010674651156443" style="display:none">Read now because of the blog event Women in Translation Month.<br /><br />I don't really know Moomin characters like many of you do: I didn't see a Moomin book until the age of 7 or 8 (and remember realising these were the Moomin things some of the other kids had been talking about) By then, they looked a bit 'babyish'. I read the then-available books very quickly and often once only. <br /><br />So reading this - recently translated to English for the first time - I had little to no idea of how different the characters' personalities were from later volumes - only that the drawings got better subsequently and Moomins became cuter and rounder. (There's still a really sweet picture of one asleep here.) I don't know if the teenage boy in the lighthouse is a proto-Snufkin. (I found out a few months ago that Snufkin was a popular character to have childhood crushes on - much less embarrassing than my equivalents, as I used to think we could grow up to be cartoon characters of different species.)<br /><br />This is a Quest story and there's a new mini-adventure and a new near-deus-ex character almost every double page. Are books for small kids usually like that? <br />(Some of the memorable short term characters included the man with the forest of sweets - if this wasn't the first translation, one might assume he inspired Roald Dahl; the [teenage] tulip girl with blue hair; and the very silly aggressive ant-lion who likes kicking sand at people.)<br />It's all a lot of fun, (sometimes it's almost as strange as <i>Yellow Submarine</i>) though I did think it a bit too trusting, not always explaining why they throw their lot in with people, and absolutely everyone turning out to be alright. (But then you get a similar propensity to assume people will be trustworthy in feelgood modern Scandinavian films.)<br />Having heard how some parents find certain kids' books encourage children to be a nuisance (Horrid Henry, is one, I believe), Moomins must be a nice contrast. They are not boring, but they are still polite, and not destructive.<br /><br />I'm not the right type of much-too-old reader for kids' books: I question too many things. (I asked nerdy awkward questions as a child, but didn't notice so many things.) Was pleased that some of my questions were answered by the book: it turns out that Moominmama and Moomintroll were going through the forest looking for somewhere to build a home, because Moomins traditionally lived behind stoves, but couldn't tolerate central heating, and moved outdoors when their families got it installed. So they are a kind of friendly archaic household spirit! And that makes me like them more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13669010674651156443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14748375571796160438">Despite being a massive Moonin fan when I was a kid, for some reason I never ended up reading the books. I'm trying to fix that now. And what's a better start than the first Moomin book ever?<br/><br/><i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> is a short story of Moomintroll and Moominmamma searching for Moominpappa, who's gone off adventuring with Hattifatteners. Along their journey, Moomintroll and Moominmamma meet curious creatures and persons, and find themselves in scary as well as in peculiar places. Tove's dr</span>
  <span id="freeText14748375571796160438" style="display:none">Despite being a massive Moonin fan when I was a kid, for some reason I never ended up reading the books. I'm trying to fix that now. And what's a better start than the first Moomin book ever?<br /><br /><i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> is a short story of Moomintroll and Moominmamma searching for Moominpappa, who's gone off adventuring with Hattifatteners. Along their journey, Moomintroll and Moominmamma meet curious creatures and persons, and find themselves in scary as well as in peculiar places. Tove's drawings and paintings really makes this book come alive.<br /><br />This was an odd read for someone who've seen the animated TV show for hundreds of times, but it was still very interesting as this was the book that started it all. And it already has many unique elements that are familiar in the later Moomin installments. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523799053" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23121713-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376567869p2/23121713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523799053?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/23121713-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Miyazaki fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523799053" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4243646922852020804">Delightful, charmingly illustrated little story. The first time I was introduced to Moomins was by a uni friend only about 5 years ago. I watched one episode and thought it was bizarre, a little scary and intriguing. After that brief introduction, I thought I'd look into this Moomins fairytale and I can't help but feel a little sad that Moomins were not part of my childhood. Like a Scandinavian Miyazaki, Tove Jansson's Moomin characters and world feel both real and fanciful. Though simple in sty</span>
  <span id="freeText4243646922852020804" style="display:none">Delightful, charmingly illustrated little story. The first time I was introduced to Moomins was by a uni friend only about 5 years ago. I watched one episode and thought it was bizarre, a little scary and intriguing. After that brief introduction, I thought I'd look into this Moomins fairytale and I can't help but feel a little sad that Moomins were not part of my childhood. Like a Scandinavian Miyazaki, Tove Jansson's Moomin characters and world feel both real and fanciful. Though simple in style, the story subtly reveals full characters with personalities.<br />A minute grievance: I wouldn't have named this story <i>The Moomins and the Great Flood</i> considering how little a part the flood plays. Something about finding a home might have been more fitting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4243646922852020804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_495059180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495059180" />
    <a title="A.E. Shaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7436627-a-e-shaw"><img alt="A.E. Shaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442628177p2/7436627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495059180?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A.E. Shaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A.E. Shaw" href="/user/show/7436627-a-e-shaw">A.E. Shaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7436627-a-e-shaw?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495059180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1439154287861699932"><br/>I know I tried to read the Moomin stories when I was little, but something about them felt very bleak, and very scary, and I just couldn't. And then the TV series really gave me the fear. It wasn't until I went and spent a considerable amount of time in Finland and Sweden that I thought I ought to give them another go, for they are so very beloved, even by my nearest and dearest, and still I'd refused to read them. So, after watching the lovely, lovely BBC4 documentary about Tove Jansson the oth</span>
  <span id="freeText1439154287861699932" style="display:none"><br />I know I tried to read the Moomin stories when I was little, but something about them felt very bleak, and very scary, and I just couldn't. And then the TV series really gave me the fear. It wasn't until I went and spent a considerable amount of time in Finland and Sweden that I thought I ought to give them another go, for they are so very beloved, even by my nearest and dearest, and still I'd refused to read them. So, after watching the lovely, lovely BBC4 documentary about Tove Jansson the other day, I thought, it is time to fix this at long last. <br /><br />I'm glad I waited, but I'm glad I got around to them, too. Or, around to starting, for this is the first I've read. Knowing, or, understanding, more about the context in which the first books were written, it really does help with appreciating the darkness and also the sweetness of them. <br /><br />There's no doubt that the imagination in here is vast, and delightful. Peculiar characters are introduced so lightly and easily that no matter their strangeness, you know who they are and what they're like in a sentence and a picture or two. <br /><br />I feel this is the right time for Moomin and his family, and I, to become good friends. I hope the others are as delightful as this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1439154287861699932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1179704564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179704564" />
    <a title="Stephen Curran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran"><img alt="Stephen Curran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574349718p2/11677504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179704564?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Curran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Curran" href="/user/show/11677504-stephen-curran">Stephen Curran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179704564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16094209440308326233">Aside from hazy memories of the animations being on television when I was a child, I am a new arrival in Moominland. I read elsewhere that even though The Moomins and the Great Flood is the first book in the series, it is not recommended as an introduction: the main characters arriving fully formed later on. This was the first story to be written but the last to be translated into English. Nevertheless, I was won over.<br/><br/>Given that it was written in 1945, it is perhaps unsurprising that it is a tal</span>
  <span id="freeText16094209440308326233" style="display:none">Aside from hazy memories of the animations being on television when I was a child, I am a new arrival in Moominland. I read elsewhere that even though The Moomins and the Great Flood is the first book in the series, it is not recommended as an introduction: the main characters arriving fully formed later on. This was the first story to be written but the last to be translated into English. Nevertheless, I was won over.<br /><br />Given that it was written in 1945, it is perhaps unsurprising that it is a tale of devastation, with divided families and displaced persons facing terrifying ordeals. The Moomins, looking for a home, cross an inhospitable land to find their missing father. Mostly, though, it is a classic adventure story, heightened by beautiful descriptions of nature and Tove Jansson's charming, touching illustrations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16094209440308326233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=adoption">adoption</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=nonsense">nonsense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=translation">translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42270985-mathew?shelf=nature">nature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352246342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16790411938045728315">Tove Jansson's first novel for children, published in '45 carries with it the sense of tension and foreboding that she herself felt at the dawn of war. Moominmamma and Moomintroll enter the dark wood in the hope of finding a new home and some sunlight. Their journey takes them to some magical places where they meet some wonderfully original and vivid creatures until they hear word that Moomintroll's father, who had gone missing, may be close by. This story powerfully evokes a sense of danger and</span>
  <span id="freeText16790411938045728315" style="display:none">Tove Jansson's first novel for children, published in '45 carries with it the sense of tension and foreboding that she herself felt at the dawn of war. Moominmamma and Moomintroll enter the dark wood in the hope of finding a new home and some sunlight. Their journey takes them to some magical places where they meet some wonderfully original and vivid creatures until they hear word that Moomintroll's father, who had gone missing, may be close by. This story powerfully evokes a sense of danger and hostility within a dark world; yet Moominmamma's wonderful resolve and deep love for all those under her care act as a guiding light throughout. Children will love all the different settings and creatures that they would encounter. It's a story, an author and a world that I have fallen for: big time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16790411938045728315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Janssonâs desire to escape the bleak realities of the war spawned a nostalgic and comforting world to which to retreat. A simple dawdle in the wind, a distraction, a hark back to the forests and valleys of childhood resulted in the Moomins family, who filled the hearts of children with a fuzzy warmth during a time of great cold.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wKDwT1R4Dor4gnYJNGMA2c8wqgC6wmnYXNjnUBAJa5jlD1IqKxw6tSxJNrVZBxr/3N6M4DQCzqYxa1H3cq+bEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">About Tove Jansson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1419249529p3/45230.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/45230.Tove_Jansson">Tove Jansson
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,423
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13433185602076867671"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br/><br/>Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br/><br/>Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText13433185602076867671" style="display:none"><b>Tove Jansson</b> was born and died in Helsinki, Finland. As a Finnish citizen whose mother tongue was Swedish, she was part of the Swedish-speaking Finns minority. Thus, all her books were originally written in Swedish.<br /><br />Although known first and foremost as an author, Tove Jansson considered her careers as author and painter to be of equal importance. <br /><br />Tove Jansson wrote and illustrated her first <i>Moomin</i> book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3300083-the-moomins-and-the-great-flood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Moomins and the Great Flood</a> (1945), during World War II. She said later that the war had depressed her, and she had wanted to write something naive and innocent. Besides the <i>Moomin</i> novels and short stories, Tove Jansson also wrote and illustrated four original and highly popular picture books.<br /><br />Jansson's <i>Moomin</i> books have been translated into 33 languages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13433185602076867671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
